TITLE: Streamlit Pages: Multi-Page App Structure
DESCRIPTION: An experimental component for structuring Streamlit applications into multiple pages. It allows defining pages with their respective file paths, titles, and icons. Requires the st-pages library.

SOURCE: https://docs.streamlit.io/develop/api-reference_slug=deploy&slug=tutorials&slug=www.streamlit

LANGUAGE: python
CODE:
```
from st_pages import Page, show_pages, add_page_title

show_pages([
    Page("streamlit_app.py", "Home", ""),
    Page("other_pages/page2.py", "Page 2", ":books:"),
])
```

TITLE: Streamlit Toggle Set Value
DESCRIPTION: Demonstrates how to set the value of the st.toggle widget. This example shows setting the toggle to 'True' and running the widget.

TITLE: Initialize AppTest from Function
DESCRIPTION: Explains how to initialize `st.testing.v1.AppTest` from a Python function that contains the Streamlit app code. This facilitates testing of modular Streamlit components.

SOURCE: https://docs.streamlit.io/develop/api-reference_slug=get-started&slug=fundamentals&slug=www.streamlit

LANGUAGE: Python
CODE:
```
from streamlit.testing.v1 import AppTest

at = AppTest.from_function(app_script_as_callable)
at.run()
```

TITLE: Create a SQL Database Connection

LANGUAGE: Python
CODE:
```

st.dataframe(pet_owners)

TITLE: Initialize AppTest with a Function
DESCRIPTION: Illustrates initializing an AppTest instance with a Python function that generates the Streamlit application. This allows for dynamic creation of testable apps.

SOURCE: https://docs.streamlit.io/develop/api-reference/app-testing/st.testing

LANGUAGE: Python
CODE:
```
from streamlit.testing.v1 import AppTest

def my_streamlit_app():
    import streamlit as st
    st.title("Dynamic App")

# Initialize AppTest with a function that defines the Streamlit app
app_test = AppTest.from_function(my_streamlit_app)
```

TITLE: Streamlit Lottie Animation
DESCRIPTION: Integrates Lottie animations into Streamlit applications, allowing for dynamic and engaging visual elements. Requires loading animation data from a URL.

```

TITLE: Build an LLM App using LangChain and OpenAI with Streamlit
DESCRIPTION: This tutorial demonstrates how to develop a chat application leveraging the LangChain framework and OpenAI's models within the Streamlit environment.

SOURCE: https://docs.streamlit.io/develop/tutorials/chat-and-llm-apps

LANGUAGE: Python
CODE:
```
import streamlit as st
from langchain_openai import ChatOpenAI
from langchain_core.messages import HumanMessage, SystemMessage

# Initialize the LLM
llm = ChatOpenAI(model="gpt-3.5-turbo")

st.title("LangChain Chat App")

# Initialize chat history
if "langchain_messages" not in st.session_state:
    st.session_state.langchain_messages = [
        SystemMessage(content="You are a helpful assistant.")
    ]

# Display chat messages from history on app rerun
for message in st.session_state.langchain_messages:
    if isinstance(message, HumanMessage):
        with st.chat_message("user"):
            st.markdown(message.content)
    elif isinstance(message, SystemMessage):
        st.sidebar.write(f"System: {message.content}")
    else: # Assuming AssistantMessage
        with st.chat_message("assistant"):
            st.markdown(message.content)

# Accept user input
if prompt := st.chat_input("Ask LangChain something"):
    # Add user message to chat history
    st.session_state.langchain_messages.append(HumanMessage(content=prompt))
    # Display user message in chat message container
    with st.chat_message("user"):
        st.markdown(prompt)
    # Get assistant response
    with st.chat_message("assistant"):
        response = llm.invoke(st.session_state.langchain_messages)
        st.markdown(response.content)
    # Add assistant response to chat history
    st.session_state.langchain_messages.append(response)
```

TITLE: Streamlit Lottie Animation
DESCRIPTION: Integrates Lottie animations into Streamlit applications, allowing for dynamic and engaging visual elements. Requires loading animation data from a URL.

TITLE: Initialize AppTest from File
DESCRIPTION: Shows how to initialize `st.testing.v1.AppTest` from a Python file to simulate a running Streamlit app for testing purposes. It allows setting secrets and running the app.

SOURCE: https://docs.streamlit.io/en/0.68.0/api

LANGUAGE: Python
CODE:
```
from streamlit.testing.v1 import AppTest

at = AppTest.from_file("streamlit_app.py")
at.secrets["WORD"] = "Foobar"
at.run()
assert not at.exception
```

TITLE: Streamlit Mapping Demo with Pydeck
DESCRIPTION: Demonstrates geospatial data visualization using `st.pydeck_chart`. It loads data from GitHub, allows users to select map layers via checkboxes in the sidebar, and displays the map with specified view states and layers.

SOURCE: https://docs.streamlit.io/get-started/tutorials/create-a-multipage-app

LANGUAGE: Python
CODE:
```
import streamlit as st
import pandas as pd
import pydeck as pdk

from urllib.error import URLError

def mapping_demo():
    import streamlit as st
    import pandas as pd
    import pydeck as pdk

    from urllib.error import URLError

    st.markdown(f"# {list(page_names_to_funcs.keys())[2]}")
    st.write(
        """
        This demo shows how to use [`st.pydeck_chart`](https://docs.streamlit.io/develop/api-reference/charts/st.pydeck_chart) to display geospatial data. """
    )

    @st.cache_data
    def from_data_file(filename):
        url = (
            "http://raw.githubusercontent.com/streamlit/" 
            "example-data/master/hello/v1/%s" % filename
        )
        return pd.read_json(url)

    try:
        ALL_LAYERS = {
            "Bike Rentals": pdk.Layer(
                "HexagonLayer",
                data=from_data_file("bike_rental_stats.json"),
                get_position=["lon", "lat"],
                radius=200,
                elevation_scale=4,
                elevation_range=[0, 1000],
                extruded=True,
            ),
            "Bart Stop Exits": pdk.Layer(
                "ScatterplotLayer",
                data=from_data_file("bart_stop_stats.json"),
                get_position=["lon", "lat"],
                get_color=[200, 30, 0, 160],
                get_radius="[exits]",
                radius_scale=0.05,
            ),
            "Bart Stop Names": pdk.Layer(
                "TextLayer",
                data=from_data_file("bart_stop_stats.json"),
                get_position=["lon", "lat"],
                get_text="name",
                get_color=[0, 0, 0, 200],
                get_size=15,
                get_alignment_baseline="'bottom'",
            ),
            "Outbound Flow": pdk.Layer(
                "ArcLayer",
                data=from_data_file("bart_path_stats.json"),
                get_source_position=["lon", "lat"],
                get_target_position=["lon2", "lat2"],
                get_source_color=[200, 30, 0, 1ArgsConstructor(160],
                get_target_color=[200, 30, 0, 160],
                auto_highlight=True,
                width_scale=0.0001,
                get_width="outbound",
                width_min_pixels=3,
                width_max_pixels=30,
            ),
        }
        st.sidebar.markdown("### Map Layers")
        selected_layers = [
            layer
            for layer_name, layer in ALL_LAYERS.items()
            if st.sidebar.checkbox(layer_name, True)
        ]
        if selected_layers:
            st.pydeck_chart(
                pdk.Deck(
                    map_style="mapbox://styles/mapbox/light-v9",
                    initial_view_state={
                        "latitude": 37.76,
                        "longitude": -122.4,
                        "zoom": 11,
                        "pitch": 50,
                    },
                    layers=selected_layers,
                )
            )
        else:
            st.error("Please choose at least one layer above.")
    except URLError as e:
        st.error(
            """
            **This demo requires internet access.**

            Connection error: %s
            """
            % e.reason
        )

```

])
```

TITLE: Simulate a Streamlit App with AppTest
DESCRIPTION: Simulate a running Streamlit app for testing purposes using st.testing.v1.AppTest. This allows you to programmatically interact with your app and validate its behavior. You can initialize the app from a file, string, or function.

SOURCE: https://docs.streamlit.io/develop/api-reference_slug=knowledge-base&slug=dependencies&slug=www.streamlit

LANGUAGE: python
CODE:
```
from streamlit.testing.v1 import AppTest

at = AppTest.from_file("streamlit_app.py")
at.secrets["WORD"] = "Foobar"
at.run()
assert not at.exception

at.text_input("word").input("Bazbat").run()
assert at.warning[0].value == "Try again."
```

--------------------------------

TITLE: Simulate Streamlit App with AppTest
DESCRIPTION: Introduces `st.testing.v1.AppTest` for simulating a running Streamlit app during testing. It allows setting secrets, running the app, and asserting outcomes.

SOURCE: https://docs.streamlit.io/develop/api-reference_slug=develop&slug=tutorials&slug=elements&slug=www.streamlit

LANGUAGE: Python
CODE:
```
from streamlit.testing.v1 import AppTest

at = AppTest.from_file("streamlit_app.py")
at.secrets["WORD"] = "Foobar"
at.run()
assert not at.exception

at.text_input("word").input("Bazbat").run()
assert at.warning[0].value == "Try again."
```

TITLE: Streamlit Progress Bar with stqdm

  sleep(0.5)

TITLE: Display Text with st.write

LANGUAGE: Python

TITLE: Streamlit Line Chart
DESCRIPTION: Shows how to create and display a line chart in a Streamlit application using st.line_chart(). This example generates random data using NumPy and formats it into a Pandas DataFrame for plotting.

SOURCE: https://docs.streamlit.io/get-started/fundamentals/main-concepts

LANGUAGE: Python
CODE:
```
import streamlit as st
import numpy as np
import pandas as pd

chart_data = pd.DataFrame(
      np.random.randn(20, 3),
      columns=['a', 'b', 'c'])

st.line_chart(chart_data)
```

TITLE: Build Custom Streamlit Connection
DESCRIPTION: Create your own custom database or API connection for Streamlit by extending the `BaseConnection` class. This involves implementing the `_connect` method to establish the connection and a `query` method for data retrieval.

SOURCE: https://docs.streamlit.io/develop/api-reference_slug=deploy&slug=streamlit-community-cloud&slug=get-started&slug=www.streamlit

LANGUAGE: Python
CODE:
```
class MyConnection(BaseConnection[myconn.MyConnection]):
    def _connect(self, **kwargs) -> MyConnection:
        return myconn.connect(**self._secrets, **kwargs)
    def query(self, query):
        return self._instance.query(query)
```

TITLE: Initialize AppTest from File
DESCRIPTION: Shows how to initialize `st.testing.v1.AppTest` from a Python file to simulate a running Streamlit app for testing purposes. It allows setting secrets and running the app.

SOURCE: https://docs.streamlit.io/develop/api-reference_slug=api-reference&slug=data&slug=st

LANGUAGE: Python
CODE:
```
from streamlit.testing.v1 import AppTest

at = AppTest.from_file("streamlit_app.py")
at.secrets["WORD"] = "Foobar"
at.run()
assert not at.exception
```

--------------------------------

TITLE: Create Login Page Function
DESCRIPTION: Defines the 'login' function for the Streamlit app. It includes a header, a selectbox for role selection, and a button to commit the chosen role to session state and rerun the app.

SOURCE: https://docs.streamlit.io/develop/tutorials/multipage/dynamic-navigation

LANGUAGE: Python
CODE:
```
def login():
    st.header("Log in")
    role = st.selectbox("Choose your role", ROLES)
    if st.button("Log in"):
        st.session_state.role = role
        st.rerun()
```

TITLE: Style Metric Cards with Streamlit Extras

# Assuming 'col3' is a Streamlit column object

TITLE: Create Custom Connection with BaseConnection
DESCRIPTION: Provides an example of building a custom Streamlit connection by subclassing `BaseConnection`. This custom connection handles connecting to a specific service and executing queries.

SOURCE: https://docs.streamlit.io/develop/api-reference/connections

LANGUAGE: Python
CODE:
```
class MyConnection(BaseConnection[myconn.MyConnection]):
    def _connect(self, **kwargs) -> MyConnection:
        return myconn.connect(**self._secrets, **kwargs)
    def query(self, query):
        return self._instance.query(query)
```

TITLE: Simulate Streamlit App with AppTest
DESCRIPTION: Introduces `st.testing.v1.AppTest` for simulating a running Streamlit app during testing. It allows setting secrets, running the app, and asserting outcomes.

SOURCE: https://docs.streamlit.io/develop/api-reference_slug=knowledge-base&slug=deploy&slug=www.streamlit

LANGUAGE: Python
CODE:
```
from streamlit.testing.v1 import AppTest

at = AppTest.from_file("streamlit_app.py")
at.secrets["WORD"] = "Foobar"
at.run()
assert not at.exception

at.text_input("word").input("Bazbat").run()
assert at.warning[0].value == "Try again."
```

TITLE: Build Custom Streamlit Connection
DESCRIPTION: Build your own custom Streamlit connection by inheriting from `BaseConnection`. This allows integrating with various data sources or APIs not natively supported.

SOURCE: https://docs.streamlit.io/develop/api-reference_slug=get-started&slug=installation&slug=www.streamlit

LANGUAGE: Python
CODE:
```
class MyConnection(BaseConnection[myconn.MyConnection]):
    def _connect(self, **kwargs) -> MyConnection:
        return myconn.connect(**self._secrets, **kwargs)
    def query(self, query):
        return self._instance.query(query)
```

TITLE: Setting up Python Environment - GitHub Actions
DESCRIPTION: This YAML snippet configures the job environment for GitHub Actions, specifying the runner as 'ubuntu-latest' and setting up the Python version to 3.11.

SOURCE: https://docs.streamlit.io/develop/concepts/app-testing/automate-tests

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
jobs:
  streamlit:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    steps:
      - uses: actions/checkout@v4
      - uses: actions/setup-python@v5
        with:
          python-version: "3.11"
```

--------------------------------

TITLE: Connect Streamlit to MongoDB
DESCRIPTION: This guide explains how to connect Streamlit applications to MongoDB. It demonstrates using Streamlit's Secrets management for secure connection details.

SOURCE: https://docs.streamlit.io/develop/tutorials/databases

LANGUAGE: Python
CODE:
```
import streamlit as st
from pymongo import MongoClient

# Retrieve MongoDB connection details from Streamlit secrets
# Example secrets.toml:
# [mongodb]
# uri = "mongodb+srv://<username>:<password>@<cluster-url>/<database_name>?retryWrites=true&w=majority"

def get_mongo_client():
    try:
        client = MongoClient(st.secrets["mongodb"]["uri"])
        return client
    except Exception as e:
        st.error(f"Error connecting to MongoDB: {e}")
        return None

def get_mongo_collection(db_name, collection_name):
    client = get_mongo_client()
    if client:
        try:
            db = client[db_name]
            collection = db[collection_name]
            return collection
        except Exception as e:
            st.error(f"Error accessing MongoDB collection: {e}")
            return None
    return None

def find_documents_in_mongo(db_name, collection_name, query={}):
    collection = get_mongo_collection(db_name, collection_name)
    if collection:
        try:
            documents = list(collection.find(query))
            return documents
        except Exception as e:
            st.error(f"Error finding documents in MongoDB: {e}")
            return []
    return []

# Example usage:

st.title("MongoDB Document Viewer")

db_name = "mydatabase"
collection_name = "mycollection"

if st.button("Find Documents in MongoDB"):
    # Example query: find documents where 'status' is 'active'
    query = {"status": "active"}
    documents = find_documents_in_mongo(db_name, collection_name, query)
    
    if documents:
        st.write(f"Found {len(documents)} documents with status 'active':")
        for doc in documents:
            st.write(doc)
    else:
        st.write("No documents found matching the query.")

```

TITLE: Streamlit Code Block Display
DESCRIPTION: The st.code function displays a block of code, optionally with syntax highlighting. This is useful for showcasing code examples within your Streamlit application.

SOURCE: https://docs.streamlit.io/develop/api-reference_slug=knowledge-base&slug=deploy&slug=www.streamlit

LANGUAGE: Python
CODE:
```
st.code("a = 1234")
```

--------------------------------

TITLE: Streamlit Progress Bar with stqdm
DESCRIPTION: Integrates a simple progress bar into Streamlit apps using the `stqdm` library. It's designed for easy use with loops to visualize progress.

SOURCE: https://docs.streamlit.io/develop/api-reference_slug=deploy&slug=streamlit-community-cloud&slug=share-your-app&slug=www.streamlit

LANGUAGE: python
CODE:
```
from stqdm import stqdm
from time import sleep

for _ in stqdm(range(50)):
  sleep(0.5)
```

TITLE: Display a Download Button in Streamlit
DESCRIPTION: Displays a button that allows users to download a file. Requires the file content to be provided.

SOURCE: https://docs.streamlit.io/develop/api-reference_slug=develop&slug=tutorials&slug=authentication&slug=www.streamlit

LANGUAGE: Python
CODE:
```
import streamlit as st

# Assuming 'file' contains the file content
# file = ...
st.download_button("Download file", file)
```

TITLE: Streamlit TextArea Input
DESCRIPTION: Demonstrates how to use the st.text_area widget to get multi-line text input from the user. It takes a string input and runs the operation.

SOURCE: https://docs.streamlit.io/develop/api-reference_slug=develop&slug=www.streamlit

LANGUAGE: Python
CODE:
```
at.text_area[0].input("Streamlit is awesome!").run()
```

--------------------------------

TITLE: Configure Streamlit Page Settings
DESCRIPTION: Provides an example of using `st.set_page_config()` to customize the Streamlit application's page title, favicon, and other default settings. This function should be called only once at the beginning of your app.

SOURCE: https://docs.streamlit.io/develop/api-reference/configuration

LANGUAGE: python
CODE:
```
st.set_page_config(
    page_title="My app",
    page_icon=":shark:",
)
```

--------------------------------

TITLE: Streamlit Audio Playback
DESCRIPTION: Integrates an audio player to play audio files. Supports NumPy arrays, audio bytes, files, and URLs, with options for format specification.

SOURCE: https://docs.streamlit.io/develop/api-reference_slug=develop&slug=tutorials&slug=authentication&slug=www.streamlit

LANGUAGE: Python
CODE:
```
st.audio(numpy_array)
st.audio(audio_bytes)
st.audio(file)
st.audio("https://example.com/myaudio.mp3", format="audio/mp3")
```

TITLE: Get User Info in Streamlit
DESCRIPTION: Returns information about a logged-in user using Streamlit's built-in authentication. Requires Streamlit.

SOURCE: https://docs.streamlit.io/develop/api-reference_slug=develop&slug=tutorials&slug=elements&slug=www.streamlit

LANGUAGE: python
CODE:
```
if st.user.is_logged_in:
    st.write(f"Welcome back, {st.user.name}!")
```

TITLE: Interact with Streamlit Sidebar in Tests

LANGUAGE: Python
CODE:
```
# at.sidebar returns a Block
at.sidebar.button[0].click().run()
assert not at.exception
```

TITLE: Get Image Coordinates with Streamlit
DESCRIPTION: Retrieves the coordinates of clicks on an image displayed in a Streamlit app. Requires the 'streamlit-image-coordinates' library.

SOURCE: https://docs.streamlit.io/develop/api-reference_slug=develop&slug=api-reference&slug=data&slug=st.column_config&slug=www.streamlit

LANGUAGE: Python
CODE:
```
from streamlit_image_coordinates import streamlit_image_coordinates

value = streamlit_image_coordinates("https://placekitten.com/200/300")
st.write(value)
```

TITLE: Streamlit Lottie Animation
DESCRIPTION: Integrates Lottie animations into Streamlit applications, allowing for dynamic and engaging visual elements. Requires loading animation data from a URL.

SOURCE: https://docs.streamlit.io/develop/api-reference_slug=develop&slug=tutorials&slug=chat-and-llm-apps&slug=www.streamlit

LANGUAGE: Python
CODE:
```
from streamlit_lottie import st_lottie

lottie_hello = load_lottieurl("https://assets5.lottiefiles.com/packages/lf20_V9t630.json")

st_lottie(lottie_hello, key="hello")
```

TITLE: Initialize AppTest from Function
DESCRIPTION: Explains how to initialize `st.testing.v1.AppTest` from a Python function that contains the Streamlit app code. This facilitates testing of modular Streamlit components.

SOURCE: https://docs.streamlit.io/develop/api-reference_slug=develop&slug=tutorials&slug=chat-and-llm-apps&slug=www.streamlit

LANGUAGE: Python
CODE:
```
from streamlit.testing.v1 import AppTest

at = AppTest.from_function(app_script_as_callable)
at.run()
```

--------------------------------

TITLE: Create a SQL Database Connection
DESCRIPTION: Establish a connection to a SQL database using Streamlit's connection API. This allows querying and interacting with the database.

SOURCE: https://docs.streamlit.io/develop/api-reference_slug=knowledge-base&slug=dependencies&slug=www.streamlit

LANGUAGE: Python
CODE:
```
conn = st.connection('pets_db', type='sql')
pet_owners = conn.query('select * from pet_owners')
st.dataframe(pet_owners)
```

--------------------------------

TITLE: Streamlit Embed with Multiple Options
DESCRIPTION: This example illustrates combining multiple embed options to customize the embedding behavior of a Streamlit app, including toolbar, padding, footer, colored line, and disabled scrolling.

SOURCE: https://docs.streamlit.io/deploy/streamlit-community-cloud/share-your-app/embed-your-app

LANGUAGE: URL
CODE:
```
/?embed=true&embed_options=show_toolbar&embed_options=show_padding&embed_options=show_footer&embed_options=show_colored_line&embed_options=disable_scrolling
```

TITLE: Style Metric Cards with Streamlit Extras
DESCRIPTION: Applies custom styling to metric cards in Streamlit using the 'streamlit-extras' library. This example shows styling a metric component.

SOURCE: https://docs.streamlit.io/develop/api-reference_slug=deploy&slug=www.streamlit

LANGUAGE: Python
CODE:
```
from streamlit_extras.metric_cards import style_metric_cards

# Assuming 'col3' is a Streamlit column object
col3.metric(label="No Change", value=5000, delta=0)

style_metric_cards()
```

TITLE: Streamlit Pyplot Deprecation Warning
DESCRIPTION: Starting December 1st, 2020, st.pyplot() will require a figure. To disable the deprecation warning, set deprecation.showPyplotGlobalUse to False.

SOURCE: https://docs.streamlit.io/develop/quick-reference/release-notes/2020

LANGUAGE: Python
CODE:
```
import streamlit as st

# To disable the warning:
# st.set_option('deprecation.showPyplotGlobalUse', False)

# Example usage (will require a figure after Dec 1st, 2020):
# import matplotlib.pyplot as plt
# fig, ax = plt.subplots()
# st.pyplot(fig)
```

TITLE: Streamlit Pages: Multi-Page App Structure
DESCRIPTION: An experimental component for structuring Streamlit applications into multiple pages. It allows defining pages with their respective file paths, titles, and icons. Requires the st-pages library.

SOURCE: https://docs.streamlit.io/develop/api-reference_slug=develop&slug=tutorials&slug=multipage&slug=www.streamlit

LANGUAGE: python
CODE:
```
from st_pages import Page, show_pages, add_page_title

show_pages([
    Page("streamlit_app.py", "Home", ""),
    Page("other_pages/page2.py", "Page 2", ":books:"),
])
```

TITLE: Initialize AppTest from File
DESCRIPTION: Initialize a simulated Streamlit app from a file using st.testing.v1.AppTest.from_file. This allows you to load your app's code from a Python file for testing. The AppTest object provides methods for interacting with the app.

SOURCE: https://docs.streamlit.io/develop/api-reference_slug=knowledge-base&slug=dependencies&slug=www.streamlit

LANGUAGE: python
CODE:
```
from streamlit.testing.v1 import AppTest

at = AppTest.from_file("streamlit_app.py")
at.run()
```

DESCRIPTION: Demonstrates how to use the auth0-component to quickly add comprehensive user login functionality to Streamlit applications. It requires a client ID and domain for authentication.

LANGUAGE: Python
CODE:
```
from auth0_component import login_button
user_info = login_button(clientId, domain = domain)
st.write(user_info)
```

TITLE: Deploy Streamlit App on Kubernetes
DESCRIPTION: This section covers deploying Streamlit applications on Kubernetes. It would typically involve creating Kubernetes deployment and service manifests to manage the application's lifecycle and network access.

SOURCE: https://docs.streamlit.io/knowledge-base/deploy/deploy-streamlit-heroku-aws-google-cloud

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: Deployment
metadata:
  name: streamlit-app
spec:
  replicas: 3
  selector:
    matchLabels:
      app: streamlit-app
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: streamlit-app
    spec:
      containers:
      - name: streamlit-app
        image: your-dockerhub-username/your-streamlit-app:latest
        ports:
        - containerPort: 8501
---
apiVersion: v1
kind: Service
metadata:
  name: streamlit-app-service
spec:
  selector:
    app: streamlit-app
  ports:
    - protocol: TCP
      port: 80
      targetPort: 8501
  type: LoadBalancer
```

CODE:
```
import streamlit as st

TITLE: Convert TOML to Environment Variable (Example)
DESCRIPTION: Explains the convention for converting Streamlit configuration options from TOML format to environment variables. Section headers and option names are converted to upper snake case with a `STREAMLIT_` prefix.

SOURCE: https://docs.streamlit.io/develop/concepts/configuration/options

LANGUAGE: python
CODE:
```
# TOML:
# [client]
# showErrorDetails = true

# Environment Variable:
# STREAMLIT_CLIENT_SHOW_ERROR_DETAILS=true
```

--------------------------------

DESCRIPTION: Illustrates how to fetch a specific configuration option from Streamlit's settings using the `st.get_option` function. This is useful for accessing theme colors or other app-wide settings.

SOURCE: https://docs.streamlit.io/develop/api-reference_slug=deploy&slug=streamlit-community-cloud&slug=get-started&slug=www.streamlit

LANGUAGE: Python
CODE:
```
st.get_option("theme.primaryColor")
```

--------------------------------

TITLE: Upgrade Streamlit with Pipenv
DESCRIPTION: This snippet shows how to upgrade Streamlit using Pipenv. It involves activating the Pipenv shell, upgrading Streamlit, and then verifying the installed version.

SOURCE: https://docs.streamlit.io/knowledge-base/using-streamlit/how-upgrade-latest-version-streamlit

LANGUAGE: Shell
CODE:
```
cd myproject 
pipenv shell 
pip install --upgrade streamlit 
streamlit version 
```

LANGUAGE: Shell
CODE:
```
pipenv update streamlit 
pipenv run streamlit version 
```
